  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_870aa4aa-a19c-4ef9-9850-7e65cb182b02'

<div id="review_1556063587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556063587" />
    <a title="Kellyn Roth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52072956-kellyn-roth"><img alt="Kellyn Roth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529965383p2/52072956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1556063587?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kellyn Roth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kellyn Roth" href="/user/show/52072956-kellyn-roth">Kellyn Roth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52072956-kellyn-roth?shelf=classical-reads">classical-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52072956-kellyn-roth?shelf=books-for-teens">books-for-teens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52072956-kellyn-roth?shelf=romance-general">romance-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52072956-kellyn-roth?shelf=books-for-adults">books-for-adults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52072956-kellyn-roth?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1556063587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16470191216713976962">I can never decide which of the Betsy-Tacy books are my favorite. I think that's because I love them all (especially the ones from her highschool years on) equally. They are all so sweet and perfect and I love them. But <em>Betsy's Wedding</em> has a special place in my heart.<br/><br/>Why? Well, y'know. Betsy and Joe are (big spoilers ...) married in this one. They are adorable. Like, they must be the cutest couple ever! They get along so well, and even when they disagree, they manage to get through it together. </span>
  <span id="freeText16470191216713976962" style="display:none">I can never decide which of the Betsy-Tacy books are my favorite. I think that's because I love them all (especially the ones from her highschool years on) equally. They are all so sweet and perfect and I love them. But <em>Betsy's Wedding</em> has a special place in my heart.<br /><br />Why? Well, y'know. Betsy and Joe are (big spoilers ...) married in this one. They are adorable. Like, they must be the cutest couple ever! They get along so well, and even when they disagree, they manage to get through it together. It's a hard time for a young couple to get started in the world (yet another spoiler: WW1), but they get through it together. I only wish Lovelace had written just one more book! At the end, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Joe goes off to war. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I mean, seriously?! Was there ever a worse cliffhanger in the history of books?!?!?! Yet another author I have to look up in Heaven (you know, assuming ... but I'm sure she's a Christian!) and yell at. And force to write a sequel. If one is allowed to write in Heaven ... but I'd assume you would be. :P<br /><br />And we get to see the whole Crowd settled. Tacy (ohmygosh!!!), Cab (which was cute), Carney, Sam ... we even hear Tony mentioned, I think. And of course Tib. *giggles* That was possibly the cutest subplot ever. Oh, wow, am I glad <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she didn't end up with Rocky! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He was suuuuch a stinker! No way was he husband-worthy material for Tib! But <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the guy Tib did marry was awesome for her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, I was juuuust a wee bit disappointed that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Betsy and Joe didn't have a baby. I mean, Betsy even admits on several occasions that she wants a baby, and they talk about having kids. But then they don't. I suppose it would be kinda inconvenient because of the war and all ... but still. I really wish they could've had a baby before the series ended! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So yeah. Yet another reason we need an 11th Betsy-Tacy book.<br /><br />I wonder if Lovelace just thought ten was a nice even number or ...? WELL SO IS TWELVE!!! I wouldn't complain at all. *is so sad*<br /><br />But yep, this is one of my favorite books of all time, and I just can't get enough of it! :)<br /><br />Kellyn Roth, <a href="https://reveriesreviews.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reveries Reviews</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16470191216713976962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2016551377" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2016551377" />
    <a title="Beth Bonini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3106785-beth-bonini"><img alt="Beth Bonini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444482564p2/3106785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2016551377?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Bonini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Bonini" href="/user/show/3106785-beth-bonini">Beth Bonini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=marriage">marriage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2016551377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15422659031079023339">I cannot think of any other fictional series that carries the main characters from childhood (five years old) to marriage and settled adulthood. There is something immensely satisfying about this progression, although Betsy-Tacy love and devotion being what it is, I think that most of Lovelace's fans will agree with me: I wish there were at least one more novel! We have to look to Lovelace's own life to know what happens next.<br/><br/>One of the things that I truly appreciated about this novel was the fo</span>
  <span id="freeText15422659031079023339" style="display:none">I cannot think of any other fictional series that carries the main characters from childhood (five years old) to marriage and settled adulthood. There is something immensely satisfying about this progression, although Betsy-Tacy love and devotion being what it is, I think that most of Lovelace's fans will agree with me: I wish there were at least one more novel! We have to look to Lovelace's own life to know what happens next.<br /><br />One of the things that I truly appreciated about this novel was the focus on Tib - and her two unsuccessful romances before she meets the 'right' one. The love, mutual respect and devotion of the Betsy-Joe marriage is such a great example to all of us. Somehow this book - indeed, the entire series - manages to be both realistic about life's challenges and sorrows, and yet also so full of human nature at its very best. An example which comes to mind is Betsy's reaction to having Joe's Aunt Ruth come to live with them during their first year of marriage. Her initial resentment and inner resistance gradually gives way, and she has the reward of knowing that she has not only done the right thing - but she has gained from it in ways that she couldn't have imagined. <br /><br />I had to have a good cry after finishing this beloved book. What an absolute delight to read the entire series again after so many years. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15422659031079023339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780690137330" href="/book/show/6758084-betsy-s-wedding">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369112-melody?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369112-melody?shelf=comfort-read">comfort-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82260590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18011899616316570592">9/2015 stet<br/><br/>9/2012 Such a perfectly crafted book to end the series! There's just enough hearkening back, just enough tidying up, just enough looking forward. And I don't care what the rest of you say, Sally Day is a perfectly lovely child. Perfectly lovely. <br/><br/>12/2009 I meant to luxuriate in this, the last book of the Betsy-Tacy series. But I was drawn in as deeply as ever. Joe topples mountains and swims seas for Betsy's love, and Betsy is still making lists and trying to be a better person. I hope</span>
  <span id="freeText18011899616316570592" style="display:none">9/2015 stet<br /><br />9/2012 Such a perfectly crafted book to end the series! There's just enough hearkening back, just enough tidying up, just enough looking forward. And I don't care what the rest of you say, Sally Day is a perfectly lovely child. Perfectly lovely. <br /><br />12/2009 I meant to luxuriate in this, the last book of the Betsy-Tacy series. But I was drawn in as deeply as ever. Joe topples mountains and swims seas for Betsy's love, and Betsy is still making lists and trying to be a better person. I hope it's not a spoiler to say that Betsy gets married in this book, titled as it is. Her struggles as a young wife are endearing, especially that poor meat pie she tries so hard to make. She's still a little diffident for my taste, too dependent on the men in her life, even given the times- compare and contrast the earlier Jo March- but she's who she is and I love her in spite of her girlishness. The crowd dances through this book, and the sentimental, happy ending strikes just the right tone for the end of the series.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_93168890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93168890" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42321-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388463861p2/42321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93168890?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/42321-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93168890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6395928107675150619">So it wasn't as much like <i>Anne's House of Dreams</i> as I feared it would be. Really, Tacy is the one who gets the house of dreams, and the babies. Betsy and Joe are wonderful together, even though sometimes Betsy would say something about how she wanted Joe to have the final word in all things and I would be like, harumph. But then it would be all right, because until Joe felt that Betsy approved (like in the case of his Aunt Ruth coming to stay with them), everything was wrong between them. And th</span>
  <span id="freeText6395928107675150619" style="display:none">So it wasn't as much like <i>Anne's House of Dreams</i> as I feared it would be. Really, Tacy is the one who gets the house of dreams, and the babies. Betsy and Joe are wonderful together, even though sometimes Betsy would say something about how she wanted Joe to have the final word in all things and I would be like, harumph. But then it would be all right, because until Joe felt that Betsy approved (like in the case of his Aunt Ruth coming to stay with them), everything was wrong between them. And they both continued to write, and make big plans, and Betsy learned how to cook (shades of Meg March!), though not how to sew. I was glad that Betsy was still Betsy, and that Tacy came into herself when she got married and had a home of her own, and Tib was still quirky and crazy. And I'm glad the book ended before Joe and all of the other men went off to the war, because frankly, I don't want to know what happens to them. I'm going to leave this series with Joe and Betsy dancing on the porch during Tib's wedding. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6395928107675150619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3082806360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3802525921699605323">The tenth and final book in Maud Hart Lovelace's <i>Betsy~Tacy</i> series - thank goodness for the three related <i>Deep Valley</i> books, as I don't think I'm ready for my reading experience to be over! - <u>Betsy's Wedding</u> picks up just where the previous installment, <u>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7891.Betsy_and_the_Great_World__Betsy_Tacy___9_' title='Betsy and the Great World (Betsy-Tacy, #9) by Maud Hart Lovelace' rel='nofollow noopener'>Betsy and the Great World</a>
</u>, left off. When Betsy's ship docks in New York, her estranged sweetheart, Joe Willard, is waiting for her, and the two are soon engaged. Settling near the Rays in Minneapolis (of course!), once they are married, Bets</span>
  <span id="freeText3802525921699605323" style="display:none">The tenth and final book in Maud Hart Lovelace's <i>Betsy~Tacy</i> series - thank goodness for the three related <i>Deep Valley</i> books, as I don't think I'm ready for my reading experience to be over! - <u>Betsy's Wedding</u> picks up just where the previous installment, <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7891.Betsy_and_the_Great_World__Betsy_Tacy___9_" title="Betsy and the Great World (Betsy-Tacy, #9) by Maud Hart Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">Betsy and the Great World</a>
</u>, left off. When Betsy's ship docks in New York, her estranged sweetheart, Joe Willard, is waiting for her, and the two are soon engaged. Settling near the Rays in Minneapolis (of course!), once they are married, Betsy and Joe begin their life as newlyweds.<br /><br />Delightful, charming, heartwarming: <u>Betsy's Wedding</u> was an almost completely unalloyed pleasure to read! Joe was an admirable husband, and Betsy a devoted wife. Even their trials and tribulations - Betsy's struggle to master the art of cooking (oh, that meat-pie!), and Joe's determination to earn a decent living (what a schedule!) - proved entertaining. I appreciated that, good-hearted as she may have been, Betsy was no paragon, and really had to struggle to accept the fact that Joe's Aunt Ruth would be coming to live with them. I could have lived without her belief that Joe should have the final word in all decisions (<i>"One person in a family has to have the final word. I want it to be Joe, always."</i>), but that was one of the only irritants in an otherwise engaging narrative.<br /><br />I also liked the way that Lovelace handled the issue of World War I, and the patriotic feelings of German-Americans like Tib. So many children's books from or about that period tend towards jingoism, that it was a pleasure to read an account in which the common bonds of American citizenship are paramount. As Tib explains to Betsy, at one point: <i>"Of course I love the German people. But you must remember that Grosspapa Hornik was a Forty-eighter,"</i> highlighting the fact that those qualities which led many immigrants to leave Germany and Austria in the first place, would make them loyal Americans as well.<br /><br />From Tacy's babies to Margaret's beaus, company dinners at home to dancing out, this book was just so much fun to read! I even know what the Violent Study Club is, now! Truly, a fitting end to a lovely series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3802525921699605323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_8083949" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8083949" />
    <a title="Carmen Maloy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/563625-carmen-maloy"><img alt="Carmen Maloy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1195667618p2/563625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8083949?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen Maloy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen Maloy" href="/user/show/563625-carmen-maloy">Carmen Maloy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8083949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7029118956354207996">Lovelace ends the stories of Betsy's childhood with a warmly written story about the triumphs and misadventures of being a wife. The story continues to shows Betsy's faithfulness to her family, friends, and now her husband, while giving a glimpse of life in the World War I era. Betsy's Wedding is a young adult book with charm, period grace and accuracy (Betsy is very concerned about learning to cook for her wonderful groom Joe) but also prescient in its concerns for her budding career as a write</span>
  <span id="freeText7029118956354207996" style="display:none">Lovelace ends the stories of Betsy's childhood with a warmly written story about the triumphs and misadventures of being a wife. The story continues to shows Betsy's faithfulness to her family, friends, and now her husband, while giving a glimpse of life in the World War I era. Betsy's Wedding is a young adult book with charm, period grace and accuracy (Betsy is very concerned about learning to cook for her wonderful groom Joe) but also prescient in its concerns for her budding career as a writer (a la Jo in "Little Women"). <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7898.Betsy_and_Joe__Betsy_Tacy_" title="Betsy and Joe (Betsy-Tacy) by Maud Hart Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">Betsy and Joe</a> are not only great friends; they are also very much in love. Betsy supports her husband through his blue moods and silences, while Joe supports Betsy's writing at every opportunity. Most couples would do well to emulate their example of treating each other with kindness, consideration and respect. <br /><br />One thing that always impressed me about this book is how Betsy manages to defer to Joe during times of crisis without losing her identity. In other words, she's more interested in making the relationship work than in getting her own way all the time. Joe also shows the same respect to Betsy when he knows something is important to her. Theirs is a truly beautiful relationship, one that mirrored Maud Hart Lovelace's marriage to her husband, Delos. She once wrote to a fan, "Delos and I found that marrying each other was the perfect solution to life." You can tell she meant it after reading this book. <br /><br />The Betsy-Tacy books were highly autobiographical and Lovelace perfectly captures the innocence and magic of childhood. If you read this book and love it, please read the series. It will be books that you will never forget as long as you live. I also recommend the "Betsy-Tacy Companion" which is an amazing book that disects each book and compares it to it's real-life counterparts, including pictures of the "real" Betsy, Tacy, Tib and all the gang. <br /><br />I had the pleasure of visiting "Deep Valley" (aka Mankato, Minnesota) for a Betsy-Tacy convention back in 1996. It was incredible to step back in time and enter Betsy's world. We toured the city and I was actually able to step foot in "Tacy's" bedroom and sit on the famous bench at the top of the big hill. It was truly a life-altering experience. I have to thank my sister, Julie for introducting these books to me and changing my life. <br /><br />It's obvious how much these books mean to me. My first born child was named Tacy Kelly Maloy. Please read and enjoy. They are a treasure! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7029118956354207996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3019882884309241950" style="display:none">8/08: I love this book. It's the little details about the start of their marriage that just ring so true. I also love seeing Margaret all grown up - she became one of my favorite characters in this series. I really need to track down Companions to this series and read more of the real events!</span>

  <span id="freeText15962153332517333792" style="display:none">The sweetness of a new marriage of two soulmates, surrounded by dear old friends and new kindred spirits. Followed by the bitterness of beloved young men marching off to war. Followed by my cry of “Why, oh WHY, did the author choose to end this lovely and heart-warming series on such a sad note in a minor key?” <br /><br />I just need ONE MORE book in the Betsy-Tacy series. <span id="freeTextContainer8538251248611918423">What a wonderful end to a delightful series. I thoroughly enjoyed Betsy’s first few years of marriage- something we rarely get to see girls’ lit heroines go through. Joe’s supportiveness of her writing was a nice touch, though I wish we’d seen more of her professional success. <br/><br/>Again, Lovelace can write nostalgia like no one I’ve ever read.   <span id="freeText8538251248611918423" style="display:none">What a wonderful end to a delightful series. I thoroughly enjoyed Betsy’s first few years of marriage- something we rarely get to see girls’ lit heroines go through. Joe’s supportiveness of her writing was a nice touch, though I wish we’d seen more of her professional success. <br /><br />Again, Lovelace can write nostalgia like no one I’ve ever read. When Betsy and Tacy were climbing the Big Hill, reminiscing over childhood, I felt a tightness in my own chest, as if I too were remembering our shared childhood. <br /><br />There is an unfortunate mention of a great picture, The Birth of a Nation (gross). But overall the book and the series have aged well. I look forward to returning to this series again and again. </span>

<div id="review_1487950591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1487950591" />
    <a title="Sarah TheAromaofBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50868550-sarah-thearomaofbooks"><img alt="Sarah TheAromaofBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499685146p2/50868550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1487950591?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah TheAromaofBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah TheAromaofBooks" href="/user/show/50868550-sarah-thearomaofbooks">Sarah TheAromaofBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1487950591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5996235389120514009">And here we have it–the long-awaited grand finale to the Betsy-Tacy books! <i>Betsy’s Wedding </i> fulfilled all of my desires for happy endings and brought everything together wonderfully.<br/><br/>This book would probably be more appropriately titled <i>Betsy’s Marriage</i>, as the wedding takes place within the first couple of chapters. The only slightly unbelievable part of the entire story is that Betsy and Joe have been estranged for three years, and yet decide to get married within two weeks of being reunited. B</span>
  <span id="freeText5996235389120514009" style="display:none">And here we have it–the long-awaited grand finale to the Betsy-Tacy books! <i>Betsy’s Wedding </i> fulfilled all of my desires for happy endings and brought everything together wonderfully.<br /><br />This book would probably be more appropriately titled <i>Betsy’s Marriage</i>, as the wedding takes place within the first couple of chapters. The only slightly unbelievable part of the entire story is that Betsy and Joe have been estranged for three years, and yet decide to get married within two weeks of being reunited. But still, more power to them! They settle down in Minneapolis, near Betsy’s family, and begin their life together, and it’s adorable and sweet and profound, just like the rest of the books.<br /><br />One that that has been incredibly annoying is that all the forewords of these beautiful new editions are invariably written by a rabid feminist who insists that Lovelace was a rabid feminist as well (apparently because she wrote about girls who were happy and not very good at cooking), so hopefully you will excuse me while I address a few of the issues raised on this topic.<br /><br />First off, the foreword of this book insists that Betsy is a wonderful example of a feminist because she always wanted to be a writer, not a housewife. And yet the entirety of <i>Betsy’s Wedding</i> is about Betsy being a housewife, and loving every moment of it. In fact, Betsy actually bemoans, on multiple occasions, the fact that she didn’t devote more time growing up to learning housewifely skills. At one point, Joe has been working for a lady named Mrs. Hawthorne, but has now been promoted to working for a major newspaper, owned by Mrs. Hawthorne’s husband.<br /><br /><blockquote>After dinner, when Joe’s transfer to the Courier was being discussed, Mrs. Hawthorne turned to Betsy.<br /><br />“It will be hard for me to fill Joe’s place,” she said. “Would you like to try? I know you write. You might enjoy working in a publicity office.”<br /><br />Betsy was very pleased but her answer came promptly. “Oh, Mrs. Hawthorne, I know I’d love it! Joe has told me how delightful your office is. But, Mrs. Hawthorn, I already have a job.”<br /><br />“You have?” She sounded surprised.<br /><br />“Yes. And it’s important, and very hard. It’s learning how to keep house.” </blockquote><br /><br />Ah yes, she definitely sounds like a career woman, doesn’t she?<br /><br />Later in the book, Betsy and Joe have their first real trouble when Joe’s aunt (who raised Joe) wants to come and live with them. Betsy is sad to see their happy honeymoon time broken up, and although she’s agreed, she knows that her heart is still in rebellion. And so, she goes to church to pray.<br /><br /><blockquote>Betsy dug her head into her arms. “Help me, God! Please help me!” she prayed.<br /><br />This was the first real problem of their marriage. Up to now, everything had been perfect. Her struggles with cooking, Joe’s low moods hadn’t mattered, really. This was different. This was a real disagreement.<br /><br />Joe had decided it. “But I wanted him to. one person in a family has to have the final word. I want it to be Joe, always.” </blockquote><br /><br />Betsy’s prayers help her to realize that by asking Joe to tell his aunt no, she is actually asking Joe to be less than himself–to do something that his conscience tells him would be wrong. But the point is, Betsy makes an important decision at this moment. It’s more than agreeing that Joe’s aunt can come stay. It’s acknowledging that she wants Joe to be the leader in their home. Betsy will always tell her thoughts and opinions and share her insight, and Joe will always listen, but she has decided that when it comes down to it, she wants Joe to have the final say, because she knows that a harmonious home exists when each person fills the role they were meant to play.<br /><br />All this to say–I think that Betsy is a beautiful example of true femininity. She is intelligent, she has dreams, she is true to herself, she is independent, but she also embraces her role as a housewife, prioritizes her husband and household’s needs above her own, and in general tries to mature into a true woman–changing and shaping her character because that’s what maturity does: it changes us from selfish, self-absorbed, self-adulating children, into outward-focused, selfless adults.<br /><br />The feminist of the foreword (Anne Quindlen, if you’re interested) insists that Betsy (and, consequently, Lovelace) was a feminist because she had dreams and aspirations. But I believe that that simply makes her a person. It is Betsy’s goodness and yearning to do what’s right that helps her to grow into a woman. Betsy becomes content and happy with her life when she is filling the role of a help meet–for Joe, for her parents, for her friends–because Betsy has learned that dreams are good and beautiful, but that no shame is to be found in simple loving service.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5996235389120514009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_224542323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224542323" />
    <a title="Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1850370-lawrence"><img alt="Lawrence" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224542323?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lawrence" href="/user/show/1850370-lawrence">Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780690137330" href="/book/show/6758084-betsy-s-wedding">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224542323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5566985151104493656">This book is a triumphant finale to Miss Lovelace's series on Betsy (and Tacy and Tib). From the beginning when Betsy and Joe meet at the dock to the very end with its sweet valedictory to Hill Street, the book is a perfect whole. Betsy at last finds a reality that grounds her affectionate and enthusiastic nature. Miss Lovelace describes very well Betsy's observant intelligence as she both learns to cook, for example, and closely examines the "first apartment's" elm tree through the seasons. In </span>
  <span id="freeText5566985151104493656" style="display:none">This book is a triumphant finale to Miss Lovelace's series on Betsy (and Tacy and Tib). From the beginning when Betsy and Joe meet at the dock to the very end with its sweet valedictory to Hill Street, the book is a perfect whole. Betsy at last finds a reality that grounds her affectionate and enthusiastic nature. Miss Lovelace describes very well Betsy's observant intelligence as she both learns to cook, for example, and closely examines the "first apartment's" elm tree through the seasons. In this book, Betsy does not write; instead, she uses her time in simply living and, as I recollect, at least begins to turn to writing what she knows best --- her own life. I also appreciated the realistic portrayal of Betsy's reluctance to take in Aunt Ruth whom she at first regards as an intruder into the closed world of a new marriage. Betsy works this out well by self examination in the tradition of Carney on the hill at Vassar.<br /><br />I feel that this book closes an entire volume on Betsy's life. Yet, I do not feel that I need to read another volume: The portrayal of Betsy is so strong in this last book that the reader can extrapolate her future with satisfaction on his/her own.<br /><br />I do not have the feeling that the book closes a volume on Joe's life. Joe remains essentially the same achieving, productive, intelligent, determined, etc., person that he seems to have been throughout his life. Nonetheless, the book reveals previously undisclosed sides to his person. One is the certain humorous, teasing quality that Betsy evokes. Here, the freedom to tease reveals his complete confidence in his feelings for her and in her. Another is his affection and sense of loyalty and gratitude to his past which is revealed in just the few pages regarding Aunt Ruth's migration to Minneapolis. His desire to invite Aunt Ruth into his and Betsy's home, of course, sets off the first faint discord in the new marriage. Here, his sadness and conflict are well depicted, albeit briefly, until the coherence of his and Betsy's values open up the future.<br /><br />This book presents Miss Lovelace's writing at its best. She can depict adult love as grounded and growing. She is able to portray happiness without the baggage of melodrama. Sometimes, she can bring tears as in her many descriptions of Betsy and Joe's courteous tenderness. The environment --- apartment and house, for example --- are well described and become characters that motivate and complement action. This is a very fine book.<br /><br />P.s. Ms. Lovelace also wrote adult fiction. Has anyone read any of it? For example, "The Black Angels" or "Early Candlelight" as referenced in the list in my copy of "Betsy's Wedding"?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5566985151104493656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13989075335542801779">Betsy is coming home from her visit around the Great World (her father sent her to Europe in the hopes it would help expand her horizons and train her as a writer). All she can think about is Joe. And there he is, cane in hand, hair so blonde it's almost silver, meeting her at the boat. <br/><br/>This Betsy-Tacy novel is both heartwarming and heartbreaking. In many ways Joe is the perfect husband. Adoring, ambitious, kind. But in other ways married life is not easy. Joe gets into dark moods. And when he i</span>
  <span id="freeText13989075335542801779" style="display:none">Betsy is coming home from her visit around the Great World (her father sent her to Europe in the hopes it would help expand her horizons and train her as a writer). All she can think about is Joe. And there he is, cane in hand, hair so blonde it's almost silver, meeting her at the boat. <br /><br />This Betsy-Tacy novel is both heartwarming and heartbreaking. In many ways Joe is the perfect husband. Adoring, ambitious, kind. But in other ways married life is not easy. Joe gets into dark moods. And when he is feeling blue he almost forgets that Betsy exists. <br /><br />Betsy, as usual, has challenges of her own. She is so self-centered and self-absorbed that she forgets to open her heart to Joe's aunt when she needs her most. A visit to church sets her on the right path and Joe's aunt living with them while she is grieving the loss of her store ends up being one of the best thing that happens to the young couple.<br /><br />Tacy has a baby and an attentive husband. But Tib. Poor Tib. Diminutive, professional, impatient, gorgeous, Tib is tired of young men thinking she is dumb and easy because she is blonde and petite. She goes through a lot of trials in this book, as Betsy and Tacy hold their breath watching. <br /><br />Highly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13989075335542801779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_16865346" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16865346" />
    <a title="Susann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/959531-susann"><img alt="Susann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204475578p2/959531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16865346?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susann" href="/user/show/959531-susann">Susann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780690137330" href="/book/show/6758084-betsy-s-wedding">review of another edition</a>

<div id="review_606938748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/606938748" />
    <a title="Nell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12459994-nell"><img alt="Nell" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/606938748?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nell" href="/user/show/12459994-nell">Nell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer606938748&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer606938748" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14690077361329130028">I read "Betsy-Tacy" and "Betsy-Tacy and Tib" when I was in grade school, and I liked them a lot. I felt like Tib really added something to the close friendship that Betsy and Tacy (there's a nickname for Anastasia that you don't hear anymore!) had formed. And I enjoyed living vicariously through Betsy's "Great World" adventures, even though I'd never read about her high school or college years. <br/><br/>Now she's back in town, newly engaged to Joe, and he wants to put a ring on it ASAP. And so he does, w</span>
  <span id="freeText14690077361329130028" style="display:none">I read "Betsy-Tacy" and "Betsy-Tacy and Tib" when I was in grade school, and I liked them a lot. I felt like Tib really added something to the close friendship that Betsy and Tacy (there's a nickname for Anastasia that you don't hear anymore!) had formed. And I enjoyed living vicariously through Betsy's "Great World" adventures, even though I'd never read about her high school or college years. <br /><br />Now she's back in town, newly engaged to Joe, and he wants to put a ring on it ASAP. And so he does, within hours of her arrival, and makes it an actual wedding band! Then he quits his job and vows to marry her as soon as possible. But, oops! Betsy's father wants his future son-in-law to be employed AND have his permission to marry her. In the shortest job hunt ever, Joe lands a new journalist gig, spends two hours talking to Mr. Ray, and the wedding's still on....in twenty-four hours!<br /><br />Despite being a last-minute event, everything is perfect and beautiful and goes off without a hitch. Then they move into a new apartment and Mr. Ray sends them a truckload of groceries as a housewarming presents. Larks! Then Tacy dares to have a baby son, instead of the daughter she's been promising Betsy. And he's ugly! Woe! But then he gets prettier, and all is forgiven.<br /><br />Then, of course, Betsy and Tacy get to be Smug Married Women together and decide to make still-not-married, independent Tib their new matchmaking project...all because they are OBSESSED with being bridesmaids at her wedding. Really, they talk about it like being a bride was just a second-best option, as was being EACH OTHER'S bridesmaids, and the true matrimonial privilege is being TIB MUELLER'S MOTHERF***ING BRIDESMAIDS. Nothing else will do!<br /><br />So they set Tib up with an older millionaire. It doesn't work out.<br /><br />Then a narcissistic newspaper man sweeps Tib off her feet. It doesn't work out.<br /><br />When her friends finally despair of marrying her off, THEN she meets the perfect guy,dates him for three weeks, and gets engaged. Betsy and Tacy act like she just singlehandedly ended world hunger.<br /><br />When America enters the First World War in 1917, Joe enlists in the Army. Betsy tries to hide how miserable this makes her, and gets a newspaper job to help with the war effort. Joe reassures her that he'll come back and they'll start a family. Tacy has another baby and Tib has a military-themed wedding. We never find out if Joe really does make it through the war, because the book ends at Tib's wedding reception. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14690077361329130028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_838940615" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838940615" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1788674-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432902126p2/1788674.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/838940615?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/1788674-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1788674-jill?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1788674-jill?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1788674-jill?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer838940615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8250827760780001560">Oh Betsy. This charming turn of the 20th century Minnesotan girl satisfied all my comfort reading desires: old-fashioned and Midwestern families; a childhood sweetheart-cum-adult lover; gobs of buttery, meaty, potatoey food porn; silk dresses, hair ribbons, and fur muffs; and most importantly, girls with ambition, girls who aspire to be more than a wife. <br/><br/>It is that last point that ended up marring the series for me. Throughout the ten books, we watch Betsy grow from age 5 to age 25. The one cons</span>
  <span id="freeText8250827760780001560" style="display:none">Oh Betsy. This charming turn of the 20th century Minnesotan girl satisfied all my comfort reading desires: old-fashioned and Midwestern families; a childhood sweetheart-cum-adult lover; gobs of buttery, meaty, potatoey food porn; silk dresses, hair ribbons, and fur muffs; and most importantly, girls with ambition, girls who aspire to be more than a wife. <br /><br />It is that last point that ended up marring the series for me. Throughout the ten books, we watch Betsy grow from age 5 to age 25. The one constant is her love for writing. She may be distracted by various beaux, but she returns to her writing again and again, aspiring to make her living by selling stories to the magazines. But in <i>Betsy’s Wedding</i> she largely abandons that goal and turns to wifely pursuits: darning and mending clothes; matchmaking her single and independent friend Tib against her interests; and preparing the best pot roast in the world for dear Joe, whose income supports the family. There are superficial references to Betsy’s writing but it’s all secondary. Betsy is now all about being a good wife. <br /><br />It’s an incredible disappointment. Somewhat unexpected too considering the level of biographic influence on these novels. Maud Hart Lovelace’s own life inspired the series (a favorite part of reading them was the back matter which detailed the fictional characters’ real life names). It’s then surprising that Betsy is so enfeebled at the story’s end considering Maud herself found remarkable career success with these books. <br /><br />I had fun reading these books and witnessing Betsy’s various scrapes with Tacy and Tib (Tib! who will always be my favorite no-nonsense German waif!) but they will not supersede the <i>Little House</i> or <i>Anne of Green Gables</i> books as my favorite old-timey comfort reads. Oh Betsy, how I wish I could have loved you like Anne and Laura. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8250827760780001560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13058778559200280895">Rereading the last book in a beloved favorite series, this is the one about what it's like for Betsy to be a newlywed. The brief honeymoon, their first home, furniture shopping and cooking disasters. Betsy and Joe are obviously in love. As much as this is Betsy's story, it is also Tacy and Tib's. Especially Tib, it is her story of being a single working girl in Minneapolis. She goes out dancing; she dates but cannot find Mr. Right.   <span id="freeText13058778559200280895" style="display:none">Rereading the last book in a beloved favorite series, this is the one about what it's like for Betsy to be a newlywed. The brief honeymoon, their first home, furniture shopping and cooking disasters. Betsy and Joe are obviously in love. As much as this is Betsy's story, it is also Tacy and Tib's. Especially Tib, it is her story of being a single working girl in Minneapolis. She goes out dancing; she dates but cannot find Mr. Right. Being the good friends they are, Betsy and Tacy who is now a mother attempt to find her a husband, Will they? Can they keep Tib safe when one of her suitors acts inappropriately? <br />What makes rereading the Betsy-Tacy series most interesting is discovering details that I had forgotten. In this one, I had forgotten about Aunt Ruth coming to live with newlyweds Joe and Betsy. And like <i>Betsy and the Great World</i>, the events in Europe (i.e. World War I) are on everyone's mind, especially Tib's. She is a German-American, can she and her family prove they are loyal to America? Is it possible for the United States stay out of the War? <br />A satisfying conclusion to a beloved series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13058778559200280895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18256879734657710531">Another Yuletide re-read! This is the last book in the Betsy-Tacy series and, despite the title, is far more about the marriage than the wedding. Which I love! I'm such a sucker for what happens after the "happy ending." And it seems to me to depict marriage in a very realistic way. They have problems, but work through them. And it's really awesome to see Betsy pursue her writing ambition at a time when women were mostly housewives.<br/><br/>And it's set right before the US's entrance into World War I, so</span>
  <span id="freeText18256879734657710531" style="display:none">Another Yuletide re-read! This is the last book in the Betsy-Tacy series and, despite the title, is far more about the marriage than the wedding. Which I love! I'm such a sucker for what happens after the "happy ending." And it seems to me to depict marriage in a very realistic way. They have problems, but work through them. And it's really awesome to see Betsy pursue her writing ambition at a time when women were mostly housewives.<br /><br />And it's set right before the US's entrance into World War I, so that adds a nice layer of tension to the book.<br /><br /><b>Re-read November 2014</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3043014816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3043014816" />
    <a title="Kiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36504237-kiana"><img alt="Kiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567452711p2/36504237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3043014816?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiana" href="/user/show/36504237-kiana">Kiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36504237-kiana?shelf=decent-or-even-good-sequels">decent-or-even-good-sequels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36504237-kiana?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36504237-kiana?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3043014816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1308738255852790619">Did anyone else find it super amusing that after five books’ worth of Betsy and Joe only sharing a couple of brief, tantalizing scenes, this book just opened with them meeting after years of silence and Joe saying, “Let’s get married next week”? It’s like Lovelace suddenly got tired of the slow build-up and fast-forwarded like nobody’s business.<br/><br/>Truthfully, I think that <i>this</i> book should have been titled <i>Betsy and Joe</i> rather than the eighth installment—because this is definitely where Betsy and Jo</span>
  <span id="freeText1308738255852790619" style="display:none">Did anyone else find it super amusing that after five books’ worth of Betsy and Joe only sharing a couple of brief, tantalizing scenes, this book just opened with them meeting after years of silence and Joe saying, “Let’s get married next week”? It’s like Lovelace suddenly got tired of the slow build-up and fast-forwarded like nobody’s business.<br /><br />Truthfully, I think that <i>this</i> book should have been titled <i>Betsy and Joe</i> rather than the eighth installment—because this is definitely where Betsy and Joe’s relationship comes to life and Joe actually feels like a fully-developed character. I know that Lovelace didn’t meet her husband (upon whom Joe is based) until after high school so the Betsy/Joe scenes in previous books were fictionalized whereas this book drew from Lovelace’s actual married life, and I think the difference really shows. Joe is so much more outspoken and sassy than any of the other books ever hinted, and watching him and Betsy learn their way through their first couple years of marriage is really sweet. <br /><br />Like the rest of the series, <i>Betsy’s Wedding</i> is unfailingly pure and kindhearted, but I feel like in many ways it’s a step up from its predecessors because the changes that the characters encounter are so significant. My concerns stemming from <i>Betsy and the Great World</i> were addressed here—the book does a better job than the previous one at balancing the cute daily incidents with the bigger changes going on with World War I, and it even ends on a slightly ominous note (much to many readers’ chagrin). The only place where the book really backslides is in Betsy and Tacy’s determination to marry off Tib despite Tib being perfectly happy in her single existence—yes, I know that it was a different era, etc., but the fact that both Betsy and Tacy, who dreamed of seeing the world and having grand adventures, criticize Tib for just living her best life rather than settling down and being a housewife read as really sour to me. <br /><br />Still, it’s a worthy ending to this series and, when one looks back on how the series began with Betsy and Tacy meeting as five-year-olds, concluding with the girls as married, responsible women (with Tacy even being a mother) is a pretty impressive feat. It might even be my favorite entry in the series, and that’s definitely not a bad way to go out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1308738255852790619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {

      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('95vVUSPPLzvVOMoLUCnnQ6C7c49zQSShnDGB8xJK+AtLo9JxLPgSWZlsyuzDIRUry83rOzwijmCgDcjMCF8DUA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+wqXT0LOR9FUZAigLjXSaGuiZGB4JHsTy26nuawf5c5HMpBvTfl6sxgwCEe9PSAAANT81DdH0dL3Uu6GtgoelQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4680075805820606791">Maud Hart Lovelace was born on April 25, 1892, in Mankato, Minnesota. She was the middle of three children born to Thomas and Stella (Palmer) Hart. Her sister, Kathleen, was three years older, and her other sister, Helen, was six years younger. “That dear family" was the model for the fictional Ray family.<br/><br/>Maud’s birthplace was a small house on a hilly residential street several blocks above Mankat</span>
  <span id="freeText4680075805820606791" style="display:none">Maud Hart Lovelace was born on April 25, 1892, in Mankato, Minnesota. She was the middle of three children born to Thomas and Stella (Palmer) Hart. Her sister, Kathleen, was three years older, and her other sister, Helen, was six years younger. “That dear family" was the model for the fictional Ray family.<br /><br />Maud’s birthplace was a small house on a hilly residential street several blocks above Mankato’s center business district. The street, Center Street, dead-ended at one of the town’s many hills. When Maud was a few months old, the Hart family moved two blocks up the street to 333 Center. <br /><br />Shortly before Maud’s fifth birthday a “large merry Irish family" moved into the house directly across the street. Among its many children was a girl Maud’s age, Frances, nicknamed Bick, who was to be Maud’s best friend and the model for Tacy Kelly. <br /><br />Tib’s character was based on another playmate, Marjorie (Midge) Gerlach, who lived nearby in a large house designed by her architect father. Maud, Bick, and Midge became lifelong friends. Maud once stated that the three couldn’t have been closer if they’d been sisters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4680075805820606791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

</a>
